padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Swisscom TV <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047488">.mw-parser-output .nobold{font-weight:normal}</style><span class="nobold">(Switzerland)</span></div></th><td class="infobox-data">Channel arbitrary</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Eir_(telecommunications)" title="Eir (telecommunications)">Eir Vision</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li>Channel 204 (SD)</li>\n<li>Channel 205 (+1)</li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #efefef;"><a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">Streaming media</a></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/All_4" title="All 4">All 4</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="nowrap"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.channel4.com/now/c4">Watch live</a></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/TVPlayer" title="TVPlayer">TVPlayer</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tvplayer.com/watch/channel4">Watch live</a> (UK only)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Sky_Go" title="Sky Go">Sky Go</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><div style="display:inline-block; padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://go.sky.com/">Watch live</a>&#160;(UK and Ireland only)</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Virgin TV Anywhere</th><td class="infobox-data"><div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://anywhere.virginmedia.com/channels/live/channel-4/">Watch live</a>&#160;(UK only)</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://anywhere.virginmedia.com/channels/live/channel-4-plus1/">Watch live</a>&#160;(+1, UK only)</li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Channel 4</b> is a British <a href="/wiki/Free-to-air" title="Free-to-air">free-to-air</a> public-service television network with a remit to produce "high quality and distinctive programming". Its headquarters are in <a href="/wiki/124_Horseferry_Road" title="124 Horseferry Road">London</a>, a National HQ in <a href="/wiki/Majestic_Cinema,_Leeds" class="mw-redirect" title="Majestic Cinema, Leeds">Leeds</a> and creative hubs in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The channel was established to provide a fourth television service to the United Kingdom in addition to the <a href="/wiki/Television_licence" title="Television licence">licence</a>-funded <a href="/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">BBC One</a> and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">BBC Two</a>, and the single commercial broadcasting network <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a>.\nIt began transmission on 2 November 1982, the day after <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh language</a> broadcaster <a href="/wiki/S4C" title="S4C">S4C</a>\'s launch. Although largely commercially self-funded, it is ultimately publicly owned; originally a subsidiary of the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Broadcasting_Authority" title="Independent Broadcasting Authority">Independent Broadcasting Authority</a> (IBA),<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> the station is now owned and operated by <a href="/wiki/Channel_Four_Television_Corporation" title="Channel Four Television Corporation">Channel Four Television Corporation</a>, a public corporation of the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Digital,_Culture,_Media_and_Sport" title="Department for Digital, Culture, Media and Sport">Department for Digital, Culture, Media and Sport</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> which was established in 1990 and came into operation in 1993. In 2010, Channel 4 extended service into Wales and became a UK-wide television channel.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 class="toctext">Religious programmes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Film"><span class="tocnumber">5.8</span> <span class="toctext">Film</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Wank_Week"><span class="tocnumber">5.9</span> <span class="toctext">Wank Week</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Ahmadinejad&#39;s_Christmas_speech"><span class="tocnumber">5.11</span> <span class="toctext">Ahmadinejad\'s Christmas speech</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#4Talent"><span class="tocnumber">5.12</span> <span class="toctext">4Talent</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-25"><a href="#4Talent_Magazine"><span class="tocnumber">5.12.1</span> <span class="toctext"><i>4Talent Magazine</i></span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Presentation"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Presentation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#On-air_identity"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">On-air identity</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Regions/International"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Regions/International</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Future_possibility_of_regional_news"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Future possibility of regional news</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Channel_4_HD"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Channel 4 HD</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#All_4"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">All 4</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Teletext_services"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Teletext services</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#4-Tel/FourText"><span class="tocnumber">11.1</span> <span class="toctext">4-Tel/FourText</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Teletext_on_4"><span class="tocnumber">11.2</span> <span class="toctext">Teletext on 4</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Awards_and_nominations"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Awards and nominations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Channel_4" title="Timeline of Channel 4">Timeline of Channel 4</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conception">Conception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Conception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fourth_UK_television_service" title="Fourth UK television service">Fourth UK television service</a></div>\n<p>Before Channel 4 and S4C, Britain had three terrestrial television services: <a href="/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">BBC1</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">BBC2</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Act_1980" title="Broadcasting Act 1980">Broadcasting Act 1980</a> began the process of adding a fourth; Channel 4 was formally created, along with its <a href="/wiki/S4C" title="S4C">Welsh counterpart</a>, by an <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Parliament" title="Act of Parliament">Act of Parliament</a> in 1982. After some months of test broadcasts, it began scheduled transmissions on 2 November 1982.\n</p><p>The notion of a second commercial broadcaster in the United Kingdom had been around since the inception of ITV in 1954 and its subsequent launch in 1955; the idea of an "ITV2" was long expected and pushed for. Indeed, television sets sold throughout the 1970s and early 1980s had a spare tuning button labelled "ITV/IBA 2". Throughout <a href="/wiki/History_of_ITV" title="History of ITV">ITV\'s history</a> and until Channel 4 finally became a reality, a perennial dialogue existed between the <a href="/wiki/General_Post_Office" title="General Post Office">GPO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">the government</a>, the ITV companies and other interested parties, concerning the form such an expansion of commercial broadcasting would take. Most likely, politics had the biggest impact in leading to a delay of almost three decades before the second commercial channel became a reality.<sup id="cite_ref-tbsseefour_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tbsseefour-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>One clear benefit of the "late arrival" of the channel was that its frequency allocations at each transmitter had already been arranged in the early 1960s, when the launch of an ITV2 was highly anticipated.<sup id="cite_ref-tbsseefour_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tbsseefour-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> This led to very good coverage across most of the country and few problems of interference with other UK-based transmissions; a stark contrast to the problems associated with <a href="/wiki/Channel_5_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Channel 5 (UK)">Channel 5</a>\'s launch almost 15 years later.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> "ITV2" is not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/ITV2" title="ITV2">ITV\'s digital television channel</a> launched in 1998.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wales">Wales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Wales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/S4C" title="S4C">S4C</a></div>\n<p>At the time the fourth service was being considered, a movement in Wales lobbied for the creation of dedicated service that would air Welsh-language programmes, then only catered for at "off peak" times on <a href="/wiki/BBC_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="BBC Wales">BBC Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/ITV_Wales_%26_West" title="ITV Wales &amp; West">HTV</a>. The campaign was taken so seriously by <a href="/wiki/Gwynfor_Evans" title="Gwynfor Evans">Gwynfor Evans</a>, former president of <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a>, that he threatened the government with a hunger strike were it not to honour the plans.<sup id="cite_ref-seefour_wales_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seefour_wales-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The result was that Channel 4 as seen by the rest of the United Kingdom would be replaced in Wales by <a href="/wiki/S4C" title="S4C">Sianel Pedwar Cymru</a> (S4C) ("Channel Four Wales"). Operated by <a href="/wiki/S4C_Authority" title="S4C Authority">a specially created authority</a>, S4C would air programmes in Welsh made by HTV, the BBC and independent companies. Initially limited frequency space meant that Channel 4 could not be broadcast alongside S4C, though some Channel 4 programmes would be aired at less popular times on the Welsh variant; this practice continued until the closure of S4C\'s analogue transmissions in 2010, at which time S4C became a fully Welsh channel.\nWith this conversion of the <a href="/wiki/Wenvoe_transmitting_station" title="Wenvoe transmitting station">Wenvoe</a> transmitter group in Wales to digital terrestrial broadcasting on 31 March 2010, Channel 4 became a UK-wide television channel for the first time.\n</p><p>Since then, carriage on digital <a href="/wiki/Cable_television" title="Cable television">cable</a>, <a href="/wiki/Satellite_television" title="Satellite television">satellite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Digital_terrestrial" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital terrestrial">digital terrestrial</a> has introduced Channel 4 to Welsh homes where it is now universally available.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_and_IBA_control">Launch and IBA control</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Launch and IBA control">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The first voice heard on Channel 4\'s opening day of Tuesday 2 November 1982 was that of <a href="/wiki/Continuity_announcer" class="mw-redirect" title="Continuity announcer">continuity announcer</a> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Coia" title="Paul Coia">Paul Coia</a> who said:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Good afternoon. It\'s a pleasure to be able to say to you, welcome to Channel Four.<sup id="cite_ref-RTC42012_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RTC42012-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>Following the announcement, the channel headed into a montage of clips from its programmes set to the station\'s signature tune, "Fourscore", written by <a href="/wiki/Lord_David_Dundas" title="Lord David Dundas">David Dundas</a>, which would form the basis of the station\'s jingles for its first decade. The first programme to air on the channel was the teatime game show <i><a href="/wiki/Countdown_(game_show)" title="Countdown (game show)">Countdown</a></i>, at 16:45 produced by <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Yorkshire Television">Yorkshire Television</a>. The first person to be seen on Channel 4 was <a href="/wiki/Richard_Whiteley" title="Richard Whiteley">Richard Whiteley</a> with <a href="/wiki/Ted_Moult" title="Ted Moult">Ted Moult</a> being the second. The first woman on the channel, contrary to popular belief, was not Whiteley\'s <i>Countdown</i> co-host <a href="/wiki/Carol_Vorderman" title="Carol Vorderman">Carol Vorderman</a> but a lexicographer only ever identified as Mary. Whiteley opened the show with the words:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>As the countdown to a brand new channel ends, a brand new countdown begins.<sup id="cite_ref-RTC42012_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RTC42012-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>On its first day, Channel 4 also broadcast soap opera <i><a href="/wiki/Brookside" title="Brookside">Brookside</a></i>, which often ran storylines thought to be controversial; this ran until 2003.\n</p><p>At its launch, Channel 4 committed itself to providing an alternative to the existing channels, an agenda in part set out by its remit which required the provision of programming to minority groups.\n</p><p>In step with its remit, the channel became well received both by minority groups and the arts and cultural worlds during this period, especially under founding chief executive <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Isaacs" title="Jeremy Isaacs">Jeremy Isaacs</a>, where the channel gained a reputation for programmes on the contemporary arts. Channel 4 co-commissioned <a href="/wiki/Robert_Ashley" title="Robert Ashley">Robert Ashley</a>\'s ground-breaking television opera <i><a href="/wiki/Perfect_Lives" title="Perfect Lives">Perfect Lives</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> which it premiered over several episodes in 1984. The channel often did not receive mass audiences for much of this period, however, as might be expected for a station focusing on minority interest.\n</p><p>Channel 4 also began the funding of independent films, such as the <a href="/wiki/Merchant_Ivory" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchant Ivory">Merchant Ivory</a> <a href="/wiki/Docudrama" title="Docudrama">docudrama</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Courtesans_of_Bombay" title="The Courtesans of Bombay">The Courtesans of Bombay</a></i>, during this time.\n</p><p>In 1992, Channel 4 also faced its first libel case by <a href="/wiki/Jani_Allan" title="Jani Allan">Jani Allan</a>, a South African journalist, who objected to her representation in <a href="/wiki/Nick_Broomfield" title="Nick Broomfield">Nick Broomfield</a>\'s documentary <i><a href="/wiki/The_Leader,_His_Driver_and_the_Driver%27s_Wife" title="The Leader, His Driver and the Driver&#39;s Wife">The Leader, His Driver and the Driver\'s Wife</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 1993, the channel broadcast the <a href="/wiki/Television_film" title="Television film">direct-to-TV</a> documentary film <i><a href="/wiki/Beyond_Citizen_Kane" title="Beyond Citizen Kane">Beyond Citizen Kane</a></i>, in which it displayed the dominant position of the <a href="/wiki/Rede_Globo" title="Rede Globo">Rede Globo</a> television network, and discussed its influence, power and political connections in Brazil.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Channel_Four_Television_Corporation">Channel Four Television Corporation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Channel Four Television Corporation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Channel_Four_Television_Corporation" title="Channel Four Television Corporation">Channel Four Television Corporation</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Multi_coloured_4,_124_Horseferry_Road,_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Multi_coloured_4%2C_124_Horseferry_Road%2C_London.jpg/220px-Multi_coloured_4%2C_124_Horseferry_Road%2C_London.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Multi_coloured_4%2C_124_Horseferry_Road%2C_London.jpg/330px-Multi_coloured_4%2C_124_Horseferry_Road%2C_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Multi_coloured_4%2C_124_Horseferry_Road%2C_London.jpg/440px-Multi_coloured_4%2C_124_Horseferry_Road%2C_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="718" data-file-height="601" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Multi_coloured_4,_124_Horseferry_Road,_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Channel 4 headquarters, <a href="/wiki/124_Horseferry_Road" title="124 Horseferry Road">124 Horseferry Road</a>, London</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Majestic_and_Quebec_Street,_September_2020.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/The_Majestic_and_Quebec_Street%2C_September_2020.jpg/220px-The_Majestic_and_Quebec_Street%2C_September_2020.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/The_Majestic_and_Quebec_Street%2C_September_2020.jpg/330px-The_Majestic_and_Quebec_Street%2C_September_2020.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/The_Majestic_and_Quebec_Street%2C_September_2020.jpg/440px-The_Majestic_and_Quebec_Street%2C_September_2020.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3168" data-file-height="2348" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Majestic_and_Quebec_Street,_September_2020.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 2020 Channel 4 opened a new national headquarters in the redeveloped <a href="/wiki/Majestic_Cinema,_Leeds" class="mw-redirect" title="Majestic Cinema, Leeds">Majestic Building</a> on <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_Square" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds City Square">City Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>After control of the station passed from the Channel Four Television Company to the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Four_Television_Corporation" title="Channel Four Television Corporation">Channel Four Television Corporation</a> in 1993, a shift in broadcasting style took place. Instead of aiming for the fringes of society, it began to focus on the edges of the mainstream, and the centre of the mass market itself.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It began to show many US programmes in peak viewing time, far more than it had previously done. It gave such shows as <i><a href="/wiki/Friends" title="Friends">Friends</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/ER_(TV_series)" title="ER (TV series)">ER</a></i> their UK premi\xc3\xa8res.\n</p><p>In the early 2000s, Channel 4 began broadcasting reality formats such as <i><a href="/wiki/Big_Brother_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Brother (UK)">Big Brother</a></i> and obtained the rights to broadcast mass appeal sporting events like <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">horse racing</a>. This new direction increased ratings and revenues.\n</p><p>In addition, the corporation launched a number of new television channels through its new <a href="/wiki/Channel_Four_Television_Corporation#4Ventures" title="Channel Four Television Corporation">4Ventures</a> offshoot, including <a href="/wiki/Film4" title="Film4">Film4</a>, <a href="/wiki/At_the_Races" class="mw-redirect" title="At the Races">At the Races</a>, <a href="/wiki/E4_(TV_channel)" title="E4 (TV channel)">E4</a> and <a href="/wiki/More4" title="More4">More4</a>.\n</p><p>Partially in reaction to its new "populist" direction, the <a href="/wiki/Communications_Act_2003" title="Communications Act 2003">Communications Act 2003</a> directed the channel to demonstrate innovation, experimentation and creativity, appeal to the tastes and interests of a culturally diverse society, and to include programmes of an educational nature which exhibit a distinctive character.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 31 December 2004, Channel 4 launched a new look and new idents in which the logo is disguised as different objects and the 4 can be seen in an angle.\n</p><p>Under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Freeview_(UK)" title="Freeview (UK)">Freeview</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Andy_Duncan_(executive)" title="Andy Duncan (executive)">Andy Duncan</a>, 2005 saw a change of direction for Channel 4\'s digital channels. Channel 4 made E4 <a href="/wiki/Free-to-air" title="Free-to-air">free-to-air</a> on <a href="/wiki/Digital_terrestrial_television_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Digital terrestrial television in the United Kingdom">digital terrestrial television</a>, and launched a new free-to-air digital channel called More4. By October, Channel 4 had joined the Freeview consortium.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> By July 2006, Film4 had likewise become free-to-air and restarted broadcasting on digital terrestrial.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Venturing into radio broadcasting, 2005 saw Channel 4 purchase 51% of shares in the now defunct <a href="/wiki/Oneword" title="Oneword">Oneword</a> radio station with UBC Media holding on to the remaining shares. New programmes such as the weekly, half-hour <i>The Morning Report</i> news programme were among some of the new content Channel 4 provided for the station, with the name <a href="#4radio">4Radio</a> being used. As of early 2009, however, Channel 4\'s future involvement in radio remained uncertain.\n</p><p>On 2 November 2007, the station celebrated its 25th birthday. It showed the first episode of <i>Countdown</i>, an anniversary <i>Countdown</i> special, as well as <a href="/wiki/The_Big_Fat_Quiz_of_the_Year#The_Big_Fat_Anniversary_Quiz" title="The Big Fat Quiz of the Year">a special edition of <i>The Big Fat Quiz</i></a> and using the original multicoloured 1982\xe2\x80\x931996 blocks logo on presentation and idents using the Fourscore jingle throughout the day.\n</p><p>In November 2009, Channel 4 launched a week of <a href="/wiki/3D_television" title="3D television">3D television</a>, broadcasting selected programmes each night using <a href="/wiki/Stereoscopy" title="Stereoscopy">stereoscopic</a> <a href="/wiki/ColorCode_3D" class="mw-redirect" title="ColorCode 3D">ColorCode 3D</a> technology. The accompanying 3D glasses were distributed through <a href="/wiki/Sainsbury%27s" title="Sainsbury&#39;s">Sainsbury\'s</a> supermarkets.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 29 September 2015, Channel 4 revamped its presentation for a fifth time; the new branding downplayed the "4" logo from most on-air usage, in favour of using the shapes from the logo in various forms. Four new idents were filmed by <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Glazer" title="Jonathan Glazer">Jonathan Glazer</a>, which featured the shapes in various real-world scenes depicting the "discovery" and "origins" of the shapes. The full logo was still occasionally used, but primarily for off-air marketing. Channel 4 also commissioned two new corporate typefaces, "Chadwick", and "Horseferry" (a variation of Chadwick with the aforementioned shapes incorporated into its letter forms), for use across promotional material and on-air.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>On 31 October 2017, Channel 4 introduced a new series of idents continuing the theme, this time depicting the logo shapes as having formed an <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphic" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthropomorphic">anthropomorphic</a> "giant" character.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Before <a href="/wiki/Digital_terrestrial_television_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Digital terrestrial television in the United Kingdom">the digital switch-over</a>, Channel 4 raised concerns over how it might finance its public service obligations afterward. It was announced in April 2006 that Channel 4\'s digital switch-over costs would be paid for by licence fee revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 March 2007, Channel 4 announced plans to launch a music channel "4Music" as a joint venture with British media company <a href="/wiki/EMAP" class="mw-redirect" title="EMAP">EMAP</a>, which would include carriage on the <a href="/wiki/Freeview_(UK)" title="Freeview (UK)">Freeview</a> platform. On 15 August 2008, <a href="/wiki/4Music" title="4Music">4Music</a> was launched across the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Channel 4 announced interest in launching a high-definition version of Film4 on Freeview, to coincide with the launch of Channel 4 HD,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> However, the fourth HD slot was given to Channel 5 instead.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Channel 4 has since acquired a 50% stake in EMAP\'s TV business for a reported \xc2\xa328&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Channel 4 was considered for privatisation by the governments of <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">John Major</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mance_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mance-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the future of the channel was again being looked into by the government, with analysts suggesting several options for the channel\'s future.<sup id="cite_ref-Mance_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mance-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2017, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Alex_Mahon" title="Alex Mahon">Alex Mahon</a> would be the next chief executive, and would take over from <a href="/wiki/David_Abraham_(executive)" class="mw-redirect" title="David Abraham (executive)">David Abraham</a>, who left in November 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_service_remit">Public service remit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Public service remit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Channel 4 was established with, and continues to hold, a remit of public service obligations which it must fulfil. The remit changes periodically, as dictated by various broadcasting and communications acts, and is regulated by the various authorities Channel 4 has been answerable to; originally the IBA, then the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Television_Commission" title="Independent Television Commission">ITC</a> and now <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a>.\n</p><p>The preamble of the remit as per the <a href="/wiki/Communications_Act_2003" title="Communications Act 2003">Communications Act 2003</a> states that:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"/><blockquote class="templatequote">\n<p>"The public service remit for Channel 4 is the provision of a broad range of high quality and diverse programming which, in particular:\n</p>\n<ul><li>demonstrates innovation, experiment and creativity in the form and content of programmes;</li>\n<li>appeals to the tastes and interests of a culturally diverse society;</li>\n<li>makes a significant contribution to meeting the need for the licensed public service channels to include programmes of an educational nature and other programmes of educative value; and</li>\n<li>exhibits a distinctive character."<sup id="cite_ref-overview_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-licence_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-licence-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n</blockquote>\n<p>The remit also involves an obligation to provide programming for schools,<sup id="cite_ref-schools_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schools-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> and a substantial amount of programming produced outside of <a href="/wiki/Greater_London" title="Greater London">Greater London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Carriage">Carriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Carriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Channel 4 was carried from its beginning on analogue terrestrial, which was practically the only means of television broadcast in the United Kingdom at the time. It continued to be broadcast through these means until the changeover to <a href="/wiki/Digital_terrestrial_television_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Digital terrestrial television in the United Kingdom">digital terrestrial television in the United Kingdom</a> was complete. Since 1998, it has been universally available on digital terrestrial, and the <a href="/wiki/Sky_(UK_%26_Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sky (UK &amp; Ireland)">Sky</a> platform (initially encrypted, though encryption was dropped on 14 April 2008 and is now free of charge and available on the <a href="/wiki/Freesat" title="Freesat">Freesat</a> platform) as well as having been available from various times in various areas, on analogue and digital cable networks.\n</p><p>Due to its special status as a public service broadcaster with a specific remit, it is afforded free carriage on the terrestrial platforms,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> in contrast with other broadcasters such as ITV.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Channel 4 is available outside the United Kingdom where it is widely available in <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The channel is registered to broadcast within the European Union/EEA through the Luxembourg Broadcasting Regulator (ALIA).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Since 2019, it has been offered by <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Broadcasting_Service" title="British Forces Broadcasting Service">British Forces Broadcasting Service (BFBS)</a> to members of HM Forces and their families around the world,  <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Broadcasting_Service#BFBS_Television" title="British Forces Broadcasting Service">BFBS Extra</a> having previously carried a selection of Channel 4 programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Channel 4 website allows Internet users in the United Kingdom to watch Channel 4 live on the Internet. In the past some programmes (mostly international imports) were not shown. Channel 4 is also provided by <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Mobile" title="Virgin Mobile">Virgin Mobile</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Digital_Audio_Broadcasting" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital Audio Broadcasting">DAB</a> mobile TV service which has the same restrictions as the Internet live stream had. Channel 4 is also carried by the Internet TV service <a href="/wiki/TVCatchup" title="TVCatchup">TVCatchup</a><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>  and was previously carried by <a href="/wiki/Zattoo" title="Zattoo">Zattoo</a> until the operator removed the channel from its platform.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Channel 4 also makes some of its programming available "on demand" via cable and the Internet through <a href="/wiki/All_4" title="All 4">All 4</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Funding">Funding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Funding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>During the station\'s formative years, funding came from the ITV companies in return for their right to sell advertisements in their region on the fourth channel.\n</p><p>Nowadays it pays for itself in much the same way as most privately run commercial stations, i.e. through the sale of on-air advertising, programme sponsorship, and the sale of any programme content and merchandising rights it owns, such as overseas sales and video sales. For example, as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> its total revenues were \xc2\xa3925&#160;million with 91% derived from sale of advertising.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> It also has the ability to subsidise the main network through any profits made on the corporation\'s other endeavours, which have in the past included subscription fees from stations such as <a href="/wiki/E4_(TV_channel)" title="E4 (TV channel)">E4</a> and Film4 (now no longer subscription services) and its "video-on-demand" sales. In practice, however, these other activities are loss-making, and are subsidised by the main network. According to Channel 4\'s last published accounts, for 2005, the extent of this cross-subsidy was some \xc2\xa330&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The change in funding came about under the <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Act_1990" title="Broadcasting Act 1990">Broadcasting Act 1990</a> when the new corporation was afforded the ability to fund itself. Originally this arrangement left a "safety net" guaranteed minimum income should the revenue fall too low, funded by large insurance payments made to the ITV companies. Such a subsidy was never required, however, and these premiums were phased out by the government in 1998. After the link with ITV was cut, the cross-promotion which had existed between ITV and Channel 4 also ended.\n</p><p>In 2007, owing to severe funding difficulties, the channel sought government help and was granted a payment of \xc2\xa314&#160;million over a six-year period. The money was to have come from the television licence fee, and would have been the first time that money from the licence fee had been given to any broadcaster other than the BBC.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> However, the plan was scrapped by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Culture,_Media_and_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State for Culture, Media and Sport">Secretary of State for Culture, Media and Sport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Burnham" title="Andy Burnham">Andy Burnham</a>, ahead of "broader decisions about the future framework of public service broadcasting".<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The broadcasting regulator <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a> released its review in January 2009 in which it suggested that Channel 4 would preferably be funded by "partnerships, joint ventures or mergers".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Programming">Programming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Programming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Channel_4_television_programmes" title="List of Channel 4 television programmes">List of Channel 4 television programmes</a></div>\n<p>Channel 4 is a "publisher-broadcaster", meaning that it commissions or "buys" all of its programming from companies independent of itself. It was the first broadcaster in the United Kingdom to do so on any significant scale; such commissioning is a stipulation which is included in its licence to broadcast.<sup id="cite_ref-schools_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schools-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> This had the consequence of starting an industry of production companies that did not have to rely on owning an ITV licence to see their programmes air, though since Channel 4, external commissioning has become regular practice on the numerous stations that have launched since, as well as on the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> and in ITV (where a quota of 25% minimum of total output has been imposed since the <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Act_1990" title="Broadcasting Act 1990">Broadcasting Act 1990</a> came into force). Although it was the first British broadcaster to commission all of its programmes from third parties, Channel 4 was the last terrestrial broadcaster to outsource its transmission and playout operations (to <a href="/wiki/Red_Bee_Media" title="Red Bee Media">Red Bee Media</a>), after 25 years in-house.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The requirement to obtain all content externally is stipulated in its licence.<sup id="cite_ref-licence_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-licence-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, Channel 4 also began a trend of owning the copyright and distribution rights of the programmes it aired, in a manner that is similar to the major Hollywood studios\' ownership of television programmes that they did not directly produce.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Thus, although Channel 4 does not produce programmes, many are seen as belonging to it.\n</p><p>It was established with a specific intention of providing programming to groups of minority interests, not catered for by its competitors, which at the time were only the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> and <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tbsseefour_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tbsseefour-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Channel 4 also pioneered the concept of \'stranded programming\', where seasons of programmes following a common theme would be aired and promoted together. Some would be very specific, and run for a fixed period of time; the <i><a href="/wiki/4_Mation" class="mw-redirect" title="4 Mation">4 Mation</a></i> season, for example, showed innovative animation. Other, less specific strands, were (and still are) run regularly, such as <i><a href="/wiki/T4_(Channel_4)" title="T4 (Channel 4)">T4</a></i>, a strand of programming aimed at teenagers, on weekend mornings (and weekdays during school/college holidays); <i>Friday Night Comedy</i>, a slot where the channel would pioneer its style of comedy commissions, <i>4Music</i> (now a separate channel) and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=4Later&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="4Later (page does not exist)">4Later</a></i>, an eclectic collection of offbeat programmes transmitted in the early hours of the morning.\n</p><p>In its earlier years, certain risqu\xc3\xa9 art-house films (dubbed by many of Channel 4\'s critics as being pornographic) would be screened with a <i><a href="/wiki/Red_triangle_(Channel_4)" title="Red triangle (Channel 4)">red triangle</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Digital_on-screen_graphic" title="Digital on-screen graphic">digital on-screen graphic</a> in the upper right of the screen. Other films were broadcast under the <i>Film on Four</i> banner, before the <i>FilmFour</i> brand was launched in the late 1990s.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Most_watched_programmes">Most watched programmes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Most watched programmes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following is a list of the 10 most watched shows on Channel 4 since launch, based on Live +28 data supplied by <a href="/wiki/BARB" class="mw-redirect" title="BARB">BARB</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and archival data published by Channel 4.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Rank</th>\n<th>Programme or film</th>\n<th>Viewers Off">The Great British Bake Off</a></i></td>\n<td>10.03</td>\n<td>27 August 2019\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kids_Segment">Kids Segment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Kids Segment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><i>Take 5</i> (Channel 4) (1992\xe2\x80\x931996)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comedy">Comedy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Comedy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>During the station\'s early days, the screenings of innovative short one-off <a href="/wiki/Comedy_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Comedy films">comedy films</a> produced by a rotating line-up of alternative comedians went under the title of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Comic_Strip_Presents" class="mw-redirect" title="The Comic Strip Presents">The Comic Strip Presents</a></i>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tube_(TV_series)" title="The Tube (TV series)">The Tube</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Live_(UK_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saturday Live (UK TV series)">Saturday Live/Friday Night Live</a></i> also launched the careers of a number of comedians and writers. Channel 4 broadcast a number of popular American imports, including <i><a href="/wiki/Roseanne" title="Roseanne">Roseanne</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Friends" title="Friends">Friends</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sex_and_the_City" title="Sex and the City">Sex and the City</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/South_Park" title="South Park">South Park</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Will_%26_Grace" title="Will &amp; Grace">Will &amp; Grace</a></i>. Other significant US acquisitions include <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i>, for which the station was reported to have paid \xc2\xa3700,000 per episode for the terrestrial television rights.\n</p><p>In April 2010, Channel 4 became the first UK broadcaster to adapt the American comedy institution of <a href="/wiki/Roast_(comedy)" title="Roast (comedy)">roasting</a> to British television, with <i><a href="/wiki/A_Comedy_Roast" title="A Comedy Roast">A Comedy Roast</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian5Apr2010_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian5Apr2010-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Channel4AComedyRoastEpisodeGuide_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Channel4AComedyRoastEpisodeGuide-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010, Channel 4 organised <i><a href="/wiki/Channel_4%27s_Comedy_Gala" title="Channel 4&#39;s Comedy Gala">Channel 4\'s Comedy Gala</a></i>, a comedy <a href="/wiki/Benefit_concert" title="Benefit concert">benefit show</a> in aid of <a href="/wiki/Great_Ormond_Street_Hospital" title="Great Ormond Street Hospital">Great Ormond Street Children\'s Hospital</a>. With over 25 comedians appearing, it billed it as "the biggest live stand up show in United Kingdom history". Filmed live on 30 March in front of 14,000 at <a href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena" title="The O2 Arena">The O2 Arena</a> in London, it was broadcast on 5 April.<sup id="cite_ref-Channel4Sales11Feb2010_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Channel4Sales11Feb2010-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> This has continued to 2016.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Factual_and_current_affairs">Factual and current affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Factual and current affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Channel 4 has a strong reputation for history programmes and real-life documentaries. It has also courted controversy, for example by broadcasting live the first public <a href="/wiki/Autopsy" title="Autopsy">autopsy</a> in the UK for 170 years, carried out by <a href="/wiki/Gunther_von_Hagens" title="Gunther von Hagens">Gunther von Hagens</a> in 2002, or the 2003 one-off stunt <i><a href="/wiki/Derren_Brown" title="Derren Brown">Derren Brown</a> Plays Russian Roulette Live</i>.\n</p><p>Its news service, <i><a href="/wiki/Channel_4_News" title="Channel 4 News">Channel 4 News</a></i>, is supplied by <a href="/wiki/ITN" title="ITN">ITN</a> whilst its long-standing investigative documentary series, <i><a href="/wiki/Dispatches_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dispatches (TV series)">Dispatches</a></i>, attracts perennial media attention.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FourDocs">FourDocs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: FourDocs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>FourDocs is an online documentary site provided by Channel 4. It allows viewers to upload their own documentaries to the site for others to view. It focuses on documentaries of between 3 and 5&#160;minutes. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.4docs.org.uk">The website</a> also includes an archive of classic documentaries, interviews with documentary filmmakers and short educational guides to documentary-making. It won a <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Award" title="Peabody Award">Peabody Award</a> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The site also includes a strand for documentaries of under 59 seconds, called "Microdocs".\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools_programming">Schools programming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Schools programming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Channel 4 is obliged to carry schools programming as part of its remit and licence.<sup id="cite_ref-schools_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schools-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ITV_Schools_on_Channel_4">ITV Schools on Channel 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: ITV Schools on Channel 4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ITV_Schools_On_Channel_4" class="mw-redirect" title="ITV Schools On Channel 4">ITV Schools On Channel 4</a></div>\n<p>Since 1957 ITV had produced schools programming, which became an obligation.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In 1987, five years after the station was launched, the IBA afforded ITV free carriage of these programmes during Channel 4\'s then-unused weekday morning hours. This arrangement allowed the ITV companies to fulfil their obligation to provide schools programming, whilst allowing ITV itself to broadcast regular programmes complete with advertisements. During the times in which schools programmes were aired <a href="/wiki/ITV_Central" title="ITV Central">Central Television</a> provided most of the <a href="/wiki/Continuity_(broadcasting)" title="Continuity (broadcasting)">continuity</a> with play-out originating from Birmingham.<sup id="cite_ref-itvschools_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itvschools-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Channel_4_Schools.2F4Learning"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Channel_4_Schools/4Learning">Channel 4 Schools/4Learning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Channel 4 Schools/4Learning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After the restructuring of the station in 1993, ITV\'s obligations to provide such programming on Channel 4\'s airtime passed to Channel 4 itself, and the new service became Channel 4 Schools, with the new corporation administering the service and commissioning its programmes, some still from ITV, others from independent producers.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2008, the 4Learning interactive new media commission <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160120045545/http://www.slabovia.tv/">slabovia.tv</a> was launched. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.today/20130706142013/http://www.slabovia.tv/SlabPlayer">The Slabplayer</a> online media player showing TV shows for teenagers was launched on 26 May 2008.\n</p><p>The schools programming has always had elements which differ from its normal presentational package. In 1993, the Channel 4 Schools idents featured famous people in one category, with light shining on them in front of an industrial looking setting supplemented by instrumental calming music. This changed in 1996 with the circles look to numerous children touching the screen, forming circles of information then picked up by other children. The last child would produce the channel 4 logo in the form of three vertical circles, with another in the middle and to the left containing the Channel 4 logo.\n</p><p>A present feature of presentation was a countdown sequence featuring, in 1993 a slide with the programme name, and afterwards an extended sequence matching the channel branding. In 1996, this was an extended ident with timer in top left corner, and in 1999 following the adoption of the squares look, featured a square with timer slowly make its way across the right of the screen with people learning and having fun while doing so passing across the screen. It finished with the Channel 4 logo box on the right of the screen and the name \'Channel 4 Schools\' being shown. This was adapted in 2000 when the service\'s name was changed to \'4Learning\'.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 2001, this was altered to various scenes from classrooms around the world and different parts of school life. The countdown now flips over from the top, right, bottom and left with each second, and ends with four coloured squares, three of which are aligned vertically to the left of the Channel 4 logo, which is contained inside the fourth box. The tag \'Learning\' is located directly beneath the logo. The final countdown sequence lasted between 2004 and 2005 and featured a background video of current controversial issues, overlaid with upcoming programming information. the video features people in the style of graffiti enacting the overuse of CCTV cameras, fox hunting, computer viruses and pirate videos, relationships, pollution of the seas and violent lifestyles. Following 2005, no branded section has been used for Schools programmes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_programmes">Religious programmes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Religious programmes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>From the outset, Channel 4 did not conform to the expectations of conventional religious broadcasting in the UK. John Ranelagh, first Commissioning Editor for Religion, made his priority \'broadening the spectrum of religious programming\' and more \'intellectual\' concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> He also ignored the religious programme advisory structure that had been put in place by the BBC, and subsequently adopted by ITV. Ranelagh\'s first major commission caused a furore, a three-part documentary series called <i><a href="/wiki/Jesus:_The_Evidence" title="Jesus: The Evidence">Jesus: The Evidence</a></i>. The programmes, transmitted during the Easter period of 1984, seemed to advocate the idea that the Gospels were unreliable, Jesus may have indulged in witchcraft, and that he may not have even existed. The series triggered a public outcry, and marked a significant moment in the deterioration in the relationship between the UK\'s broadcasting and religious institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Numerous genres of film-making \xe2\x80\x93 such as comedy, drama, documentary, adventure/action, romance and horror/thriller \xe2\x80\x93 are represented in the channel\'s schedule. From the launch of Channel 4 until 1998, film presentations on C4 would often be broadcast under the "Film on Four" banner.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2005, Channel 4 screened the uncut <a href="/wiki/Lars_von_Trier" title="Lars von Trier">Lars von Trier</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Idiots" title="The Idiots">The Idiots</a></i>, which includes unsimulated sexual intercourse, making it the first UK terrestrial channel to do so. The channel had previously screened other films with similar material but censored and with warnings.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 1 November 1998, Channel 4 has had a digital subsidiary channel dedicated to the screening of films. This channel launched as a paid subscription channel under the name "FilmFour", and was relaunched in July 2006 as a free-to-air channel under the current name of "<a href="/wiki/Film4" title="Film4">Film4</a>". The Film4 channel carries a wide range of film productions, including acquired and Film4-produced projects. Channel 4\'s general entertainment channels <a href="/wiki/E4_(TV_channel)" title="E4 (TV channel)">E4</a> and <a href="/wiki/More4" title="More4">More4</a> also screen feature films at certain points in the schedule as part of their content mix.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wank_Week">Wank Week</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Wank Week">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wank_Week" title="Wank Week">Wank Week</a></div>\n<p>A season of television programmes about <a href="/wiki/Masturbation" title="Masturbation">masturbation</a>, called <i>Wank Week</i>, was to be broadcast in the United Kingdom by Channel 4 in March 2007. The first show was about a <a href="/wiki/Masturbate-a-thon" title="Masturbate-a-thon">Masturbate-a-thon</a>, a public mass masturbation event, organised to raise money for the <a href="/wiki/Sexual_health" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual health">sexual health</a> charity <a href="/wiki/Marie_Stopes_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Marie Stopes International">Marie Stopes International</a>. Another film would have focused on compulsive male masturbators and a third was to feature the <a href="/wiki/Sex_education" title="Sex education">sex educator</a> Dr <a href="/wiki/Betty_Dodson" title="Betty Dodson">Betty Dodson</a>.\n</p><p>The series came under public attack from senior television figures, and was pulled amid claims of declining editorial standards and controversy over the channel\'s <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">public service broadcasting</a> credentials.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_warming">Global warming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Global warming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 8 March 2007, Channel 4 screened a highly controversial documentary, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Global_Warming_Swindle" title="The Great Global Warming Swindle">The Great Global Warming Swindle</a></i>. The programme states that global warming is "a lie" and "the biggest scam of modern times".<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The programme\'s accuracy has been disputed on multiple points, and several commentators have criticised it for being one-sided, noting that the mainstream position on global warming is supported by the scientific academies of the <a href="/wiki/G8" class="mw-redirect" title="G8">major industrialised nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Houghton_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Houghton-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> There were 246 complaints to <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a> as of 25 April 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> including allegations that the programme falsified data.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The programme has been criticised by scientists and scientific organisations, and various scientists who participated in the documentary claimed their views had been distorted.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Against_Nature_(documentary)" class="mw-redirect" title="Against Nature (documentary)">Against Nature</a></i>: An earlier controversial Channel 4 programme made by Martin Durkin which was also critical of the environmental movement and was charged by the Independent Television Commission of the UK for misrepresenting and distorting the views of interviewees by selective editing.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Greenhouse_Conspiracy" title="The Greenhouse Conspiracy">The Greenhouse Conspiracy</a></i>: An earlier Channel 4 documentary broadcast on 12 August 1990, as part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Equinox_(TV_programme)" title="Equinox (TV programme)">Equinox</a></i> series, in which similar claims were made.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Three of the people interviewed (Lindzen, Michaels and Spencer) were also interviewed in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Global_Warming_Swindle" title="The Great Global Warming Swindle">The Great Global Warming Swindle</a></i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Ahmadinejad.27s_Christmas_speech"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ahmadinejad\'s_Christmas_speech">Ahmadinejad\'s Christmas speech</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Ahmadinejad&#039;s Christmas speech">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the <i><a href="/wiki/Alternative_Christmas_message" title="Alternative Christmas message">Alternative Christmas address</a></i> of 2008, a Channel 4 tradition since 1993 with a different presenter each year, Iranian President <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad" title="Mahmoud Ahmadinejad">Mahmoud Ahmadinejad</a> made a thinly veiled attack on the United States by claiming that Christ would have been against "bullying, ill-tempered and expansionist powers".\n</p><p>The airing courted controversy and was rebuked by several human rights activists, politicians and religious figures, including <a href="/wiki/Peter_Tatchell" title="Peter Tatchell">Peter Tatchell</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:2_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Louise_Ellman" title="Louise Ellman">Louise Ellman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ron_Prosor" title="Ron Prosor">Ron Prosor</a><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and Rabbi Aaron Goldstein.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> A spokeswoman for the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">Foreign and Commonwealth Office</a> said: "President Ahmadinejad has, during his time in office, made a series of appalling anti-Semitic statements. The British media are rightly free to make their own editorial choices, but this invitation will cause offence and bemusement not just at home but among friendly countries abroad".<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, some defended Channel 4. <a href="/wiki/Stonewall_(charity)" title="Stonewall (charity)">Stonewall</a> director <a href="/wiki/Ben_Summerskill" title="Ben Summerskill">Ben Summerskill</a> stated: "In spite of his ridiculous and often offensive views, it is an important way of reminding him that there are some countries where free speech is not repressed...If it serves that purpose, then Channel 4 will have done a significant public service".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Byrne" title="Dorothy Byrne">Dorothy Byrne</a>, Channel 4\'s head of news and current affairs, also defended the station, saying: "As the leader of one of the most powerful states in the Middle East, President Ahmadinejad\'s views are enormously influential... As we approach a critical time in international relations, we are offering our viewers an insight into an alternative world view...Channel 4 has devoted more airtime to examining Iran than any other broadcaster and this message continues a long tradition of offering a different perspective on the world around us".<sup id="cite_ref-:2_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="4Talent">4Talent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 4Talent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>4Talent is an editorial branch of Channel 4\'s commissioning wing, which co-ordinates Channel 4\'s various talent development schemes for film, television, radio, new media and other platforms and provides a showcasing platform for new talent.\n</p><p>There are bases in London, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, Glasgow and <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>, serving editorial hubs known respectively as 4Talent National, 4Talent Central England, 4Talent Scotland and 4Talent Northern Ireland. These four sites include features, profiles and interviews in text, audio and video formats, divided into five zones: TV, Film, Radio, New Media and Extras, which covers other arts such as theatre, music and design. 4Talent also collates networking, showcasing and professional development opportunities, and runs workshops, masterclasses, seminars and showcasing events across the UK.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="4Talent_Magazine"><i>4Talent Magazine</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 4Talent Magazine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><i>4Talent magazine</i> is the creative industries magazine from 4Talent, which launched in 2005 as TEN4 magazine under the editorship of Dan Jones. <i>4Talent Magazine</i> is currently edited by Nick Carson. Other staff include deputy editor Catherine Bray and production editor Helen Byrne. The magazine covers rising and established figures of interest in the creative industries, a remit including film, radio, TV, comedy, music, new media and design.\n</p><p>Subjects are usually UK-based, with contributing editors based in Northern Ireland, Scotland, London and Birmingham, but the publication has been known to source international content from Australia, America, continental Europe and the Middle East. The magazine is frequently organised around a theme for the issue, for instance giving half of November 2007\'s pages over to profiling winners of the annual 4Talent Awards.\n</p><p>An unusual feature of the magazine\'s credits is the equal prominence given to the names of writers, photographers, designers and illustrators, contradicting standard industry practice of more prominent writer bylines. It is also recognisable for its \'wraparound\' covers, which use the front and back as a continuous canvas \xe2\x80\x93 often produced by guest artists.\n</p><p>Although <i>4Talent Magazine</i> is technically a newsstand title, a significant proportion of its readers are subscribers. It started life as a quarterly 100-page title, but has since doubled in size and is now published bi-annually.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presentation">Presentation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Presentation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Since its launch in 1982, Channel 4 has used the same logo which consists of a stylised numeral "4" made up of nine differently shaped blocks. The logo was designed by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Lambie-Nairn" title="Martin Lambie-Nairn">Martin Lambie-Nairn</a> and his partner [Colin Robinson] and was the first channel in the UK to depict an ident made using advanced computer generation (the first electronically generated ident was on <a href="/wiki/BBC2" class="mw-redirect" title="BBC2">BBC2</a> <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two_%27Computer_Generated_2%27_ident" title="BBC Two &#39;Computer Generated 2&#39; ident">in 1979</a>, but this was two-dimensional). It was designed in conjunction with Bo Gehring Aviation of Los Angeles and originally depicted the "4" in red, yellow, green, blue and purple. The music accompanying the ident was called "Fourscore" and was composed by David Dundas; it was later released as a single alongside a B-side, "Fourscore Two", although neither reached the UK charts. In November 1992, "Fourscore" was replaced by new music.\n</p><p>In 1996, Channel 4 commissioned Tomato Films to revamp the "4", which resulted in the "Circles" idents showing four white circles forming up transparently over various scenes, with the "4" logo depicted in white in one of the circles.\n</p><p>In 1999, Spin redesigned the logo to feature in a single square which sat on the right-hand side of the screen, whilst various stripes would move along from left to right, often lighting the squared "4" up. Like previous "Circles" idents from 1996 (which was made by Tomato Films), the stripes would be interspersed with various scenes potentially related to the upcoming programme.\n</p><p>The logo was made three-dimensional again in 2004 when it was depicted in filmed scenes that show the blocks forming the "4" logo for less than a second before the action moves away again.\n</p><p>In 2015, the logo was disassembled completely to allow the blocks to appear as parts of a nature scene, sometimes featuring a strange dancing creature and sometimes being excavated for scientific study, one being studied under a microscope and showing a <a href="/wiki/Tardigrade" title="Tardigrade">tardigrade</a>. The second wave of these idents, launched in 2017, depict a giant creature made of the "4" blocks (made to look almost like a person) interacting with everyday life, sometimes shouting the "Fourscore" theme as a foghorn.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="On-air_identity">On-air identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: On-air identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul class="gallery
