style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Channel_4_logo_2015.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Channel_4_logo_2015.svg/87px-Channel_4_logo_2015.svg.png" decoding="async" width="87" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Channel_4_logo_2015.svg/130px-Channel_4_logo_2015.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Channel_4_logo_2015.svg/174px-Channel_4_logo_2015.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="999" data-file-height="1378" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Channel 4 logo from 2015 to the present day\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Martin_Lambie-Nairn" title="Martin Lambie-Nairn">Lambie-Nairn</a> logo was the first logo of Channel 4, used from its launch on 2 November 1982 until 1996, lasting for fourteen years. The logo was re-introduced for one day only on 22 January 2021, to promote Channel 4\'s new five-part drama, <a href="/wiki/It%27s_a_Sin_(TV_series)" title="It&#39;s a Sin (TV series)">It\'s a Sin</a>, which focused on the 1980s <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="HIV/AIDS in the United Kingdom">AIDS crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> It was additionally used once on 28 December 2020 as a commemoration for Lambie-Nairn, who had died three days earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Regions.2FInternational"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions/International">Regions/International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Regions/International">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><b>Regions</b>:<br />\nChannel 4 has, since its inception, broadcast identical programmes and <a href="/wiki/Continuity_(broadcasting)" title="Continuity (broadcasting)">continuity</a> throughout the United Kingdom (excluding Wales where it did not operate on analogue transmitters). At launch this made it unique, as both the BBC and <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> had long established traditions of providing <a href="/wiki/Regional_variations" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional variations">regional variations</a> in their programming in different areas of the country. Since the launch of subsequent British television channels, Channel 4 has become typical in its lack of regional programming variations.\n</p><p>A few exceptions exist to this rule for programming and continuity:\n</p><p>Some of Channel 4\'s schools\' programming (1980s/early \'90s) was regionalised due to differences in curricula between different regions.<sup id="cite_ref-itvschools_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itvschools-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Part of Channel 4\'s remit covers the commissioning of programmes from outside London. Channel 4 has a dedicated director of nations and regions, <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Cosgrove" title="Stuart Cosgrove">Stuart Cosgrove</a>, who is based in a regional office in Glasgow. As his job title suggests, it is his responsibility to foster relations with independent producers based in areas of the United Kingdom (including Wales) outside London.\n</p><p>Advertising on Channel 4 does contain regular variation: prior to 1993, when ITV was responsible for selling Channel 4\'s advertising, each regional ITV company would provide the content of advertising breaks, covering the same transmitter area as themselves, and these breaks were often unique to that area. After Channel 4 became responsible for its own advertising, it continued to offer advertisers the ability to target particular audiences and divided its coverage area into six regions: London, South (including Wales),  Midlands, North, Northern Ireland and Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At present, Wales does not have its own advertising region, instead its viewers receive the southern region on digital platforms intentionally broadcast to the area or the neighbouring region where terrestrial transmissions spill over into Wales. Northern Ireland also has its own advertising window referred to as \'Ulster Macro\'.  <a href="/wiki/Channel_5_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Channel 5 (UK)">Channel 5</a> and <a href="/wiki/ITV_Breakfast" title="ITV Breakfast">ITV Breakfast</a> use a similar model to Channel 4 for providing their own advertising regions, despite also having a single national output of programming.\n</p><p><b>International:</b> \n</p><p>Channel 4 available within the Republic of Ireland is specifically tailored towards the Irish market with advertising and sponsorship specific to this market. The channel is registered with the broadcasting regulators in Luxembourg for terms of conduct and business within the EU/EEA while observing guidelines outlined by Ireland\'s <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Authority_of_Ireland" title="Broadcasting Authority of Ireland">BAI code</a>. Irish advertising sales are monitored by Media Link<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> in Dublin. Where Channel 4 does not hold broadcasting rights within the Republic of Ireland such programming is unavailable. For example, the series <a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)"><i>Glee</i></a> was not available on Channel 4 on Sky in Ireland due to it broadcasting on <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Media_One" title="Virgin Media One">Virgin Media One</a> within Ireland. Currently, programming available on All 4 is available within the Republic of Ireland without restrictions. The Channel 4 available elsewhere in Europe is the UK version of the channel. \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_possibility_of_regional_news">Future possibility of regional news</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Future possibility of regional news">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>With <a href="/wiki/ITV_plc" title="ITV plc">ITV plc</a> pushing for much looser requirements on the amount of regional news and other programming it is obliged to broadcast in its ITV regions, the idea of Channel 4 taking on a regional news commitment has been considered, with the corporation in talks with <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a> and ITV over the matter.<sup id="cite_ref-c4moveregional_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c4moveregional-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Channel 4 believe that a scaling-back of such operations on ITV\'s part would be detrimental to Channel 4\'s national news operation, which shares much of its resources with ITV through their shared news contractor <a href="/wiki/ITN" title="ITN">ITN</a>. At the same time, Channel 4 also believe that such an additional public service commitment would bode well in on-going negotiations with Ofcom in securing additional funding for its other public service commitments.<sup id="cite_ref-c4moveregional_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-c4moveregional-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Channel_4_HD">Channel 4 HD</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Channel 4 HD">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Channel_4HD_Logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Channel_4HD_Logo.svg/170px-Channel_4HD_Logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Channel_4HD_Logo.svg/255px-Channel_4HD_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Channel_4HD_Logo.svg/340px-Channel_4HD_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="368" data-file-height="256" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Channel_4HD_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Channel 4 HD logo used from 2007 until 2015.</div></div></div>\n<p>In mid-2006 Channel 4 ran a six-month closed trial of <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">HDTV</a>, as part of the wider <a href="/wiki/Digital_television_in_the_United_Kingdom#Freeview_HD" title="Digital television in the United Kingdom">Freeview HD</a> experiment via the <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_transmitting_station" title="Crystal Palace transmitting station">Crystal Palace transmitter</a> to London and parts of the <a href="/wiki/Home_counties" title="Home counties">home counties</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> including the use of <a href="/wiki/Lost_(2004_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lost (2004 TV series)"><i>Lost</i></a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Desperate_Housewives" title="Desperate Housewives">Desperate Housewives</a></i> as part of the experiment, as US broadcasters such as <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> already have an HDTV back catalogue.\n</p><p>On 10 December 2007, Channel 4 launched a <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">high definition television</a> <a href="/wiki/Simulcast" title="Simulcast">simulcast</a> of Channel 4 on <a href="/wiki/Sky%2B_HD" title="Sky+ HD">Sky</a>\'s digital satellite platform, after Sky agreed to contribute toward the channel\'s satellite distribution costs. It was the first full-time high definition channel from a terrestrial UK broadcaster.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 31 July 2009, Virgin Media added Channel 4 HD on channel 146 (later on channel 142, now on channel 141) as a part of the M pack.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> On 25 March 2010 Channel 4 HD appeared on <a href="/wiki/Freeview_(UK)" title="Freeview (UK)">Freeview</a> channel 52 with a placeholding caption, ahead of a commercial launch on 30 March 2010, coinciding with the commercial launch of Freeview HD.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> On 19 April 2011, Channel 4 HD was added to <a href="/wiki/Freesat" title="Freesat">Freesat</a> on channel 126.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> As a consequence, the channel moved from being <a href="/wiki/Free-to-view" title="Free-to-view">free-to-view</a> to <a href="/wiki/Free-to-air" title="Free-to-air">free-to-air</a> on satellite during March 2011. With the closure of <a href="/wiki/S4C" title="S4C">S4C Clirlun</a> in Wales on 1 December 2012, on Freeview, Channel 4 HD launched in Wales on 2 December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The channel carries the same schedule as Channel 4, broadcasting programmes in HD when available, acting as a simulcast. Therefore, SD programming is broadcast upscaled to HD.   The first true HD programme to be shown was the 1996 <a href="/wiki/Adam_Sandler" title="Adam Sandler">Adam Sandler</a> film <a href="/wiki/Happy_Gilmore" title="Happy Gilmore">Happy Gilmore</a>.  From launch until 2016 the presence of the 4HD logo on screen denoted true HD content.\n</p><p>On 1 July 2014, Channel 4 +1 HD, a HD simulcast of Channel 4 +1, launched on Freeview channel 110. It closed on 22 June 2020 to help make room on COM7 following the closure of COM8 on Freeview.\n</p><p>On 20 February 2018, Channel 4 announced that Channel 4 HD and All 4 will no longer be supplied on Freesat from Thursday 22 February 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 22 June 2020 Channel4+1 HD and 4Seven HD were removed from Freeview.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="All_4">All 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: All 4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/All_4" title="All 4">All 4</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/All_4" title="All 4">All 4</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Video_on_demand" title="Video on demand">video on demand</a> service from Channel 4, launched in November 2006 as 4oD. The service offers a variety of programmes recently shown on Channel 4, <a href="/wiki/E4_(TV_channel)" title="E4 (TV channel)">E4</a>, <a href="/wiki/More4" title="More4">More4</a> or from their archives, though some programmes and movies are not available due to rights issues.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Teletext_services">Teletext services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Teletext services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="4-Tel.2FFourText"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="4-Tel/FourText">4-Tel/FourText</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: 4-Tel/FourText">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Channel 4 originally licensed an ancillary teletext service to provide schedules, programme information and features. The original service was called 4-Tel, and was produced by Intelfax, a company set up especially for the purpose. It was carried in the 400s on <a href="/wiki/ORACLE_(teletext)" title="ORACLE (teletext)">Oracle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4Tel_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4Tel-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> In 1993, with Oracle losing its franchise to <a href="/wiki/Teletext_Ltd" class="mw-redirect" title="Teletext Ltd">Teletext Ltd</a>, 4-Tel found a new home in the 300s, and had its name shown in the header row. Intelfax continued to produce the service <sup id="cite_ref-4Tel_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4Tel-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> and in 2002 it was renamed FourText.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Teletext_on_4">Teletext on 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Teletext on 4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2003, Channel 4 awarded Teletext Ltd a ten-year contract to run the channel\'s ancillary teletext service, named Teletext on 4.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The service closed in 2008, and Teletext is no longer available on Channel 4, ITV and Channel 5.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Channel_4&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Awards and nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable" Awards</td>\n<td>Broadcaster of the Year</td>\n<td><i>Channel 4</i></td>\n<td style="background: #FDD; color: black; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="no Minute Wonder</a></i></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
